ﮔﺎﻝ ﺩﺍﻧﻴﻮﺱ، "ﻫﺴﻪ ﻣﺎﻧﺴﻮﻱ ﺷﻲ. ﺍﻧﻲ ﺩﮔّﻴﺖ ﻭﺍﺭﺳﻠﺖ ﺍﯾﻤﯿﻞ ﻟﻠﺸﺨﺺ ﺍﻟﻤﻘﺮﺏ ﻣﻨﻪ ﻭﺍﺟﻪ ﺭﺩﻭﺩ ﺟﺪﺍً ﻣﻨﺎﺳﺒﺔ. ﻟﻠﻮﮔﺖ ﺍﻟﺤﺎﺿﺮ، ﻫﺬﺍ ﺷﺎﻓﻲ ﺑﺎﺳﺘﺎﻧﻪ." (Gāl Dānyūs, "Hesse mānsawī shī. ʾAnī daggeyt waʾarsalt īmīl lil-shakhṣ al-muqarrab minnu wāja rudūd jiddan munāsiba. Lillaqt al-ḥāḍir, hādhā shāfī bastānah.")
من قبل، چاف المدير التنفيذي لشركة رينج، جيمي سيمينوف، گال الشركة بدت من وكت ما كان صوت جرس الباب مسموع من دكانُه جوا الگراج. **(Alternatively, slightly more formal):** قبل چت، حچى المدير التنفيذي لشركة رينج، جيمي سيمينوف، گال الشركة بدت وكت ما كان صوت الجرس مسموع من دكانُه بالگراج. **Explanation of choices & nuances reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic (specifically Baghdad/Central dialect):** * **من قبل (min gabel):** "Previously" - very common and natural. * **چاف (chaf):** "CEO" - borrowed from English, commonly used. Could also be *المدير التنفيذي* (al-mudeer al-tanfeezi) but *چاف* is very common in business contexts. * **گال (gal):** "Said" - the standard verb for 'to say' in Mesopotamian Arabic. * **بدت (bedet):** "Started" - standard verb. * **من وكت (min wakt):** "From a time when" - a common way to express "when" in this context, adding a bit of narrative flow. *من وكت* is preferred to just *وكت* because it sets the scene. * **ما كان (ma kan):** "Was not" - the standard negation. * **صوت جرس الباب (sawt jarras al-bab):** "The sound of the doorbell." * **مسموع (masmuu'):** "Audible/Heard." * **دكانُه (dukanuhu):** "His shop." The -*uhu* suffix is crucial to show possession. * **جوا الگراج (juwa al-garaj) / بالگراج (bil-garaj):** “in the garage” – *juwa* means inside, *bil-* is a preposition meaning 'in/at'. Both are used, *juwa* emphasizes *inside* the garage more. * **The use of the glottal stop (represented by the apostrophe ' )** is characteristic of Mesopotamian Arabic pronunciation.
سوا دربناڵ واي فاي، حجى.

.اتحاد الجمباز الأمريكي يدعم رسالة اللجنة الأولمبية الأمريكية ويوافق على الحاجة المطلقة للعائلة الأولمبية لتعزيز بيئة آمنة لجميع رياضينا
نتفق ويا بيان اللجنة الأولمبية الأمريكية گال مصلحة رياضيين و أندية و رياضتهم، چاي يكون أحسن إذا نتقدم بـ تغيير مهم داخل مؤسستنا، بدل ما نلغي اعتمادنا.
اتحاد الجمباز الأمريكي يدعم تحقيق مستقل ممكن يوضح كيف قدر يصير الإساءة اللي وصفها الناجين من لاري ناصر بشجاعة كبيرة ما تنكشف لهالقد، و يتقبل أي تغييرات ضرورية ومناسبة.
اتحاد الجمباز الأمريكي واللجنة الأولمبية الأمريكية عندهم نفس الهدف – تخلي رياضات الجمباز وغيرها آمنة قدر الإمكان للرياضيين حتى يقدروا يحققوا أحلامهم في بيئة آمنة وإيجابية وممكنة. **(ittihad al-jimbaaz al-amriki wa al-lajna al-olimpiyya al-amrikiya ‘indahum nafs al-hadaf – takhalli riyadhat al-jimbaaz wa ghayriha aamina qadr al-imkaan lil-riyadiyeen hatta yaqdaroo yihaqqiqoo ahlaamhum fi bi’a aamina wa iijabiya wa mumkinah.)** **Notes on choices reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic features:** * **"عندهم" ('indahum)** is common for "they have" in Mesopotamian Arabic, differing from some other dialects. * **“تخلي” (takhalli)** meaning “to make” or “to let” is a common verb usage in the dialect. * **“يقدروا” (yaqdaroo)** – is a very common way to say "they can" or "are able to" in the dialect. * **“ممكنة” (mumkinah)** is used to convey “empowered” in the sense of having possibilities and agency. Other translations for "empowered" exist, but this fits the context and sounds natural in the region. * The phrasing is kept relatively simple and direct, consistent with typical spoken Mesopotamian Arabic.

بصفته مستشار الأمن القومي، ساعد كارتر في معالجة الشؤون العالمية دبلوماسياً، مثل اتفاقيات كامب ديفيد، سنة ١٩٧٨؛ وتطبيع العلاقات الأمريكية الصينية خلال أواخر السبعينات؛ والثورة الإيرانية، اللي أدت لأزمة الرهائن الإيرانية، سنة ١٩٧٩؛ والغزو السوفيتي لأفغانستان، سنة ١٩٧٩.

ﮔﻮﺳﻠﻴﻨﮓ ﻭ ﺳﺘﻮﻥ ﺣﺼﻠﻮ ﻋﻠﻰ ﺗﺮﺷﻴﺢ ﻟﺄﻓﻀﻞ ﻣﻤﺜﻞ ﻭ ﻣﻤﺜﻠﺔ ﻋﻠﻰ ﺍﻟﺘﻮﺍﻟﻲ. (Gusling wa Stoon ḥaṣlu ʿala tarshīḥ li-afḍal mumaththil wa mumaththilah ʿala at-tawālī.)

إثنين أغاني من الفيلم، "أوديشن" (اللي يحلمون بالغباء) و "مدينة النجوم"، إستلموا ترشيحات لأحسن أغنية أصلية. استديو لاينزجيت إستلم ٢٦ ترشيح – أكثر من أي استديو ثاني.
بالليل فوك الأحد، الرئيس الأمريكي دونالد ترامب، ببيان وصل عن طريق الناطق الرسمي، أعلن القوات الأمريكية رح تطلع من سوريا. (Bil-leil fōg al-aḥad, ar-ra’īs al-Amrīki Dōnald Trump, bi-bayān waṣal ‘an ṭarīq an-nāṭiq ar-rasmī, a‘lan al-quwwāt al-Amrīki raḥ tiṭla‘ min Sūriya.)
اتعلن الخبر بعد ما الرئيس ترامب اتكلم بالتليفون ويه الرئيس التركي رجب طيب اردوغان.
تركيا هم بعد راح تتكفل بحراسة الدواعش اللي انَچدوا، والكلام گالوا، الدول الأوروبية ما قبلوا يرجعوهم لبلدانهم. **(Transcription: Turkiye hem ba'ad rah titkaffal bi-hiraset al-dawa'esh illi inchadu, wal-kalam galu, al-duwal al-Urubbiyye ma gablu yarj'uhoom li-buldanhoom.)** **Notes on choices made, reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic features:** * **"هم بعد" (hem ba'ad)** - This is a very common way to say "also" or "as well" in Mesopotamian Arabic, functioning as an emphasizer. * **"راح" (rah)** - A future marker (similar to "will" or "going to"). * **"تتكفل" (titkaffal)** - "To take responsibility for," "to handle," "to take over." * **"الدواعش" (al-dawa'esh)** - Common colloquial term for ISIS fighters. * **"انَچدوا" (inchadu)** – This dialectal form means "were captured" and is typical of the region. * **"والكلام گالوا" (wal-kalam galu)** - "And the statement said..." - a common way to attribute information to a source. * **"ما قبلوا" (ma gablu)** - "They refused." * **"يرجعوهم" (yarj'uhoom)** - "To return them." * **"لبلدانهم" (li-buldanhoom)** - "To their countries." This translation aims for naturalness within a Mesopotamian Arabic (specifically Iraqi/Baghdadi influenced) context. The specific dialect within Mesopotamia can have variations, but this is a widely understood phrasing.

التقرير يفتتح بدعوة لحوار مفتوح وتشكيل توافق في الولايات المتحدة حول سياسة الشرق الأوسط.
التقرير ينتقد بشدة كل جوانب سياسة السلطة التنفيذية الحالية تجاه العراق، ويطالب بتغيير مسار فوري.

چافت خانم كيرشنر أعلنت نيتها ترشح للرئاسة بمسرح الأرجنتين، نفس المكان اللي استخدمته تبدأ حملتها لسنة 2005 للسيناتو كعضو عن محافظة بوينس آيرس. **(Chaft Khānum Kirchner aʿlanat niyat-ha tarashshuh lil-ri'āsa bi-masraḥ al-Arjintīn, nafs al-makān illī istaḫdamat-hu tabdaʾ ḥamlat-ha li-sanat 2005 lil-sīnatō kaʿḍū ʿan muḥāfaẓat Bu'aynos Āyris.)** **Explanation of choices & linguistic notes:** * **چافت (Chaft):** A very common honorific prefix used in Iraqi Arabic (and broadly Mesopotamian Arabic) for “Mrs./Ms.” It's more colloquial and widely used than formal equivalents. * **أعلنت (aʿlanat):** Standard Arabic verb for “announced”, but pronounced with the Mesopotamian Arabic vowel shifts. * **نيتها (niyat-ha):** "Her intention" - standard, but pronunciation adjusted. * **ترشح (tarashshuh):** “To run (for office)” – a common and understood verb in this context. * **للرئاسة (lil-ri'āsa):** "For the presidency". * **بمسرح الأرجنتين (bi-masraḥ al-Arjintīn):** “At the Argentine Theatre”. * **نفس المكان اللي (nafs al-makān illī):** "The same place that" – "Illī" is a very common relative pronoun in Mesopotamian Arabic, replacing the more formal "alladhī." * **استخدمته (istaḫdamat-hu):** "She used it". * **تبدأ (tabdaʾ):** "To start/begin". * **حملتها (ḥamlat-ha):** "Her campaign". * **لسنة 2005 (li-sanat 2005):** “For the year 2005”. * **للسيناتو (lil-sīnatō):** "For the Senate". Loanword from Italian/English, commonly used. * **كعضو (kaʿḍū):** “As a member”. * **عن محافظة بوينس آيرس (ʿan muḥāfaẓat Bu'aynos Āyris):** "From/about the province of Buenos Aires." Again, the province name is a loanword and pronounced to fit Mesopotamian Arabic phonology. **Important Considerations:** * **Dialectal Variation:** "Mesopotamian Arabic" is a broad category. There's significant variation between Iraqi Arabic (Baghdadi, Basri, etc.), Syrian Arabic, and the dialects spoken by the Chaldean and Assyrian communities. This translation leans towards a generalized Iraqi Arabic flavor, leaning toward Baghdadi, which is often a "prestige" dialect for wider understanding. * **Register:** I've aimed for a relatively neutral, journalistic register – appropriate for an announcement like this. * **Pronunciation:** The transliteration provides a guide to pronunciation, but actual pronunciation will vary based on the speaker's specific background.

"Fihsha'" is a widely used term for obscenity and carries a stronger moral weight, typical of the region. * **"Sana al-maaliya"** - "Fiscal year" - standard translation. * **"laazim yakhassis"** – "Must dedicate/assign". "Laazim" (necessary/must) is very common in Mesopotamian dialects. "Yakhassis" is a more formal verb for allocation. * **"Muhaqqiqeen"** – "Investigators/Agents". * **"al-mawaad al-ibaahiya lil-kibaar"** - "Adult pornography" - a fairly direct and understood translation. “Kibaar” (adults) clarifies the content. * **Word order and phrasing:** The overall structure and word choice leans towards the Iraqi (Mesopotamian) dialect’s tendency towards more explicit phrasing and a common, direct style.

.حسب آخر نشرة، بينت قياسات مستوى البحر إنّ موجة تسونامي تشكّلت. وسُجّلت فعالية تسونامي واضحة بالقرب من باغو باغو ونيويه. **(Ḥasab ākhir nashra, baynat qiyāsāt mustawa al-baḥr inn mawjat tsūnāmī tashakkalat. Wa sujjilat faʿāliyyat tsūnāmī wāḍiḥa bil-qurb min Bāghū Bāghū wa Niyūyah.)** **Explanation of choices & linguistic notes reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic features:** * **حسب (Ḥasab):** "According to" - a very common and natural way to begin this type of statement in Iraqi/Mesopotamian Arabic. * **آخر نشرة (ākhir nashra):** "Latest bulletin" – direct translation, commonly used. * **بينت (baynat):** "Indicated" - uses the feminine form because it refers back to *nashra* (bulletin), which is feminine in Arabic. More idiomatic than a literal "showed." * **قياسات مستوى البحر (qiyāsāt mustawa al-baḥr):** "Sea level readings" – standard translation. * **إنّ (inn):** Emphatic particle introducing the fact that a tsunami *was* formed. * **موجة تسونامي (mawjat tsūnāmī):** "Tsunami wave" - uses the borrowed word "tsūnāmī" directly, as it's standard in news reports. * **تشكّلت (tashakkalat):** "Was generated/formed" - a good, natural verb choice. * **وسُجّلت (wa sujjilat):** "And was recorded" – passive voice common in formal Arabic and used here for a news report tone. * **فعالية (faʿāliyyat):** "Activity" – good, general term. * **واضحة (wāḍiḥa):** "Definite/Clear" – conveys the sense of "definite" in this context. * **بالقرب من (bil-qurb min):** "Near" – standard prepositional phrase. * **باغو باغو ونيويه (Bāghū Bāghū wa Niyūyah):** Transliteration of the place names, adapting to Arabic pronunciation conventions. Note the doubling of "gh" in Bāghū Bāghū. This translation aims for a formal, news-report style that would be typical of a Mesopotamian Arabic broadcast or newspaper. It also avoids overly literal translations that can sound awkward in Arabic.

الحي التاسع، اللي ميته غرقانة وصلوا لحد مترين بسبة إعصار كاترينا، هلأ المي واصلة للخصر لأن السد قريب منهم طاف. **(Ḥayy at-Tāsiʿ, illi miyto ġarqāna waṣṣlu li-ḥadd mitrayn bi-sabbat iʿṣār Katrina, halla l-may waṣṣla lil-khaṣr li-ʾann as-sadd ʾarīb minhum ṭāf.)** **Breakdown & Linguistic Notes:** * **الحي التاسع (Ḥayy at-Tāsiʿ):** "The Ninth Ward" - straightforward translation. * **اللي (illi):** A very common relative pronoun in Mesopotamian Arabic meaning "which" or "that". More common than the formal الذي (alladhi). * **ميته غرقانة (miyto ġarqāna):** “Its waters were flooded/submerged” – uses the feminine possessive pronoun (miyto) as the Ward is treated as feminine grammatically. ġarqāna is the active participle of "to drown/submerge." * **وصلوا لحد مترين (waṣṣlu li-ḥadd mitrayn):** "Reached up to two meters" – Uses the plural verb form (waṣṣlu) because it's conceptually referring to the waters. "Mitrayn" is the dual form of meter. * **بسبة (bi-sabbat):** “Because of” or “due to”. * **إعصار كاترينا (iʿṣār Katrina):** “Hurricane Katrina” – Transliteration is common for foreign names. * **هلأ (halla):** “Now” - Very common in spoken Mesopotamian Arabic. * **المي واصلة للخصر (al-may waṣṣla lil-khaṣr):** “The water reached the waist" - "Waṣṣla" again uses the plural form for stylistic flow. * **لأن (li-ʾann):** “Because.” * **السد قريب منهم طاف (as-sadd ʾarīb minhum ṭāf):** "The levee near them overflowed." – "Ṭāf" meaning "overflowed" or "floated over" is a common and natural expression for a levee being overtopped. "ʾArīb minhum" is "near them." This translation aims for naturalness and reflects the colloquial speech patterns of Mesopotamian Arabic speakers (specifically those from Iraq, Syria, and surrounding areas). There are regional variations, but this version should be widely understood.

چن القمر يِجذِب الأرض ويَسبب المد والجزر، هَچمي درب التبانة يِجذِب مجرة القوس. **(Chan al-qamar yijthib al-ardh wi-yassabib al-mad wal-jazar, hachmi darb at-tabana yijthib majarrat al-qaws.)** **Notes on Linguistic Choices & Why this is Mesopotamian Arabic:** * **چن (Chan):** Commonly used for "like" or "just as" in many Mesopotamian dialects, particularly those influenced by Turkish. Standard Arabic uses *kamā*. * **يِجذِب (Yijthib):** A common verb form for "attracts" or "pulls" widely used in Iraqi/Mesopotamian dialects, more colloquial than the Fusha equivalent. * **الأرض (Al-ardh):** Standard Arabic for "the earth," understood across all dialects. * **ويَسبب (Wi-yassabib):** "And causes" - The *wi-* conjunction is common in colloquial Arabic. The verb *yassabib* is a common colloquial formation. * **المد والجزر (Al-mad wal-jazar):** "The tide and the ebb" – standard terms, easily understood. * **هَچمي (Hachmi):** A very Mesopotamian way to emphasize "like that," or "in the same way." It adds a regional flavor. There isn't a direct equivalent in standard Arabic. * **درب التبانة (Darb at-tabana):** "Milky Way" – standard Arabic, but used in the region. * **مجرة القوس (Majarrat al-qaws):** "Sagittarius Galaxy" – Standard Arabic. * **Pronunciation:** The provided transliteration attempts to capture the sounds of a typical Mesopotamian Arabic speaker (specifically, leaning towards Iraqi dialects) . This translation prioritizes natural, colloquial phrasing that would be used by a native speaker *in* Mesopotamia, rather than a strictly formal, literary Arabic translation. It utilizes vocabulary and grammatical constructions commonly found in the region.

بعد سنة، الشخص المصاب ممكن ينقل العدوى لـ ١٠ إلى ١٥ شخص قريب منه.
چـافية، نسبة الـ XDR-TB بين كل الناس المصابين بالسلّ لسة تبدو قليلة؛ ٦,٠٠٠ من مجمل ٣٣٠,٠٠٠ شخص مصابين في أي لحظة في جنوب أفريقيا. **(Chafiya, nisbat al-XDR-TB bayn kull al-nas al-musaabeen bil-sull lissa tibdu qaleela; sittat alaf min mujam'al thalathmi’a wa thalathin alf shakhs musaabeen fi ayy lahza fi Janub Afriqya.)** **Notes on choices made, reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic features (specifically Baghdad dialect influence, as it's a central and often understood variety):** * **چافية (Chafiya):** Used for "However" – a common connective in Iraqi Arabic. It carries a similar nuance to "but" or "still." * **نسبة (Nisbat):** Standard Arabic word for "percentage" widely understood. * **الـ XDR-TB:** Generally, acronyms are used as-is, sometimes pronounced letter by letter. * **لسة (Lissa):** A very common Mesopotamian Arabic word meaning "still". It's crucial for the natural flow of the sentence. * **تبدو (Tibdu):** Meaning "seems," common and understood throughout the region. * **مجمل (Mujam'al):** Used to mean “total” or “aggregate” - sounds more natural in this context than a direct translation. * **مصابين (Musaabeen):** "infected" or "affected". * **في أي لحظة (fi ayy lahza):** "at any moment," maintains the nuance of the original English. * **جنوب أفريقيا (Janub Afriqya):** South Africa – standard Arabic name for the country.

بالـ 1956، سليانيا انتقل لِسُوِيد، و ثلث سنين بعدين اشتغل بالبوستة السويدية و صار رئيس النقّاشين هناك. **(Bil-1956, Słania intaqal li-Sweed, w thulth sineen ba'dein ishtaghal bil-bosta as-Sweediya w sar ra'ees an-naqqasheen hunaak.)** **Notes on choices & why this is "Mesopotamian" (specifically Baghdad/Central Iraqi) Arabic:** * **بالـ (Bil-)**: The use of "bil-" before the year is very common in Iraqi Arabic. * **انتقل (Intaqal)**: A standard Arabic verb for "moved" but frequently used in spoken Iraqi dialects. * **لِسُوِيد (Li-Sweed)**: "To Sweden," the pronunciation is closer to how it would sound in Iraqi Arabic than using a more formal Arabicized version. * **ثلث سنين (Thulth sineen)**: "Three years". This phrase, using "thulth" (third) is very common. * **بعدين (Ba'dein)**: "Later/Then/After," a very typical Iraqi colloquialism. * **اشتغل (Ishtaghal)**: "He worked." Standard Arabic, used broadly in Iraqi dialects. * **بالبوستة السويدية (Bil-bosta as-Sweediya)**: "At/in the Swedish Post Office." Uses "bosta" for "post office," common in Iraq. * **رئيس النقّاشين (Ra'ees an-naqqasheen)**: "Chief of the engravers." "Ra'ees" is standard for "chief/head." "Naqqash" is "engraver." * **هناك (Hunaak)**: "There." It's a common way to specify location in conversation. This translation attempts to balance accuracy with the natural flow of spoken Mesopotamian Arabic, leaning towards the commonly used vocabulary and phrasing of Baghdad/central Iraq. Regional variations within Mesopotamia would have slight differences, but this is a generally understandable translation across the region.

طابِعْه الألْفْ أوّلْ كانْ "أَعْمَال عَظِيمَة لِمُلُوك السْوِيد" لرَسَّام دَاوُد كْلُوكِرْ إِيرِنْسْتْرَالْ، سَنَة ألْفِين، وهَذَا مْدوّنْ بـ"كِتَابْ غِينِسْ للأَرْقَام القِيَاسِيَّة". **(Ṭābiʿuh al-alf awwal kān “Aʿmāl ʿaẓīma li-mulūk as-Swīd” li-rassām Dāwūd Klūkir Īrensṭrāl, sanit alfayn, wa hādhā mduw’wan b-"Kitāb Ghīnīs lil-Arqām al-Qiyāsiyya.")** **Notes on choices & linguistic features reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic:** * **طابع (Ṭābiʿ):** Common word for "stamp." * **الألف أوّل (al-alf awwal):** Literally "the thousand first," reflecting a typical way of expressing ordinal numbers with large numbers. * **لرَسَّام (li-rassām):** "By the artist" - using 'li' is very common for attribution. * **داوُد كْلُوكِرْ إِيرِنْسْتْرَالْ (Dāwūd Klūkir Īrensṭrāl):** Transliteration of the name, adapted to Mesopotamian Arabic pronunciation. The tendency is to approximate foreign sounds. * **سَنَة ألْفِين (sanit alfayn):** “Year two thousand”. Using ‘sanit’ for year is common. * **وهَذَا مْدوّنْ (wa hādhā mduw’wan):** “And this is recorded” – using ‘mduw’wan’ is a dialectal form. The “m-” prefix is a common feature in many Iraqi dialects. * **كِتَابْ غِينِسْ للأَرْقَام القِيَاسِيَّة (Kitāb Ghīnīs lil-Arqām al-Qiyāsiyya):** Transliteration and standard Arabic phrasing. This kind of borrowing and mixing is typical. * **The overall sentence structure:** A relatively literal translation to preserve the original meaning while sounding natural in Mesopotamian Arabic. Word order is flexible but generally follows a Subject-Verb-Object pattern when possible, with modifying phrases appearing before the nouns they modify.

.بعد ما صار الحادث، جيبسون انودى للمستشفى بس مات بعد شوية.
السواگ جيّ، الهُو عمره چهل وار، ما انصدم بالحادث. (As-sawwag jiyyi, al-hu omruh arba'a w shillin, ma insaddim bil-hadith.) **Explanation of Choices & Nuances:** * **السواگ جيّ (As-sawwag jiyyi):** "The truck driver." *Sawwag* is the common term for truck driver. *Jiyyi* is a demonstrative pronoun ("the"). * **الهُو (Al-hu):** "He/This one." Used here as a pronoun referring to the driver. * **عمره چهل وار (Omruh arba'a w shillin):** "His age is sixty-four." This uses the common Mesopotamian Arabic way of stating age – *arba'a w shillin* translates to “four and twenty” (4 x 20 + 4 = 64). It's a vigesimal system. * **ما انصدم (Ma insaddim):** "Was not injured/didn't get hit." This is the negation of "to be hit/injured." * **بالحادث (Bil-hadith):** "In the crash/accident." **Important Notes about Mesopotamian Arabic:** * **Dialectal Variation:** Mesopotamian Arabic is a collection of closely related dialects. There will be differences in pronunciation and even some vocabulary depending on the specific region (Baghdad, Mosul, Basra, etc.). This translation leans towards a broadly understood Baghdad/Central Iraqi dialect. * **Pronunciation:** I've provided a transliteration, but the actual sounds can be subtle and best learned by hearing a native speaker. * **Vigesimal System:** The age calculation is a core feature of this dialect.
السيارة نفسها انشالت من مكان الحادث تقريبًا الساعة وحدة الظهر بتوقيت غرينتش في نفس اليوم. (as-sayyara nafsiha inshalat min makan al-hadith taqriban al-sa'a wahda al-zuhr bi-tawqit Ghreenwitch fi nafs al-youm.)

لمّا خفّت الدِّيَنة وودّوا الجرحى للمستشفى، تقريبًا أربعين من السجناء اللي بقوا برا اتجمّعوا بالساحة ورَفضوا يِرجعوا لغرفهم. **(Transliteration: Lamma khaffat al-deeyna wa waddaw al-jurha lil-mustashfa, taqreeban arba'een min al-sijana elli baqaw barra itjamme'u bil-saha wa rafadu yirja'u li-ghurafhum.)** **Explanation of choices & linguistic notes (as a linguist, I feel this is useful context - but you only asked for the translation):** * **لمّا (Lamma):** "When" - a very common Mesopotamian Arabic connector. * **خفّت الدِّيَنة (Khaffat al-deeyna):** "The fighting lessened/ceased." "Deeyna" is a widely used term for conflict or a fight. Using a verb implying lessening is more natural than a direct "stopped" equivalent in this context. * **وودّوا الجرحى للمستشفى (Wa waddaw al-jurha lil-mustashfa):** "And they took the wounded to the hospital." "Wadda" (from the root و د ع ) means to deliver or send something to a destination - a natural way to express transport in this context. * **تقريبًا (Taqreeban):** "About/approximately." * **أربعين (Arba'een):** "Forty." * **السجناء اللي بقوا برا (Al-sijana elli baqaw barra):** "The prisoners who remained outside." "Elli" is the relative pronoun "who/which." "Barra" specifically means "outside" or "remaining" in this context. * **اتجمّعوا (Itjamme'u):** "They gathered." – common colloquial verb. * **بالساحة (Bil-saha):** "In the yard." * **ورَفضوا (Wa rafadu):** "And they refused." * **يِرجعوا (Yirja'u):** "To return." * **لغرفهم (Li-ghurafhum):** "To their cells/rooms." **Regional Nuances:** This translation leans towards a central Iraqi/Baghdadi dialect, which is often considered a base for broader understanding within Mesopotamia. There will be slight variations in pronunciation and some vocabulary choices depending on specific areas (e.g., Mosul, Basra).

چا، لو مي المي حتِصعد شُوَيّ بس كام رجلة بعد الطّوفان، المُسؤولين يِاملون حتِكون كافية تِرجِع حِيدر الرّمال اللي تآكلت ورا النّهر. **(Cha, law mee el-mee hatis'ad shwayy bas kam rajleh ba'ad al-toofan, al-mus'oolīn yamloon hatkoon kafiyah terje' heedir al-ramal illi taakalat wara al-nahr.)**
ما صدر أي تحذير من التسونامي، ووفقاً لوكالة جاكرتا للجيوفيزياء، ما راح يصدر تحذير من التسونامي لأن الزلزال ما وصل قوة 6.5. **(Ma ṣadr ay tahdhīr min al-tsunāmī, wa wifqan li-wikālat Jākartā lil-jiūfīzīyā’, mā rāḥ yaṣdur tahdhīr min al-tsunāmī li’ann al-zilzāl mā waṣal quwwat 6.5.)** **Explanation of choices reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic features:** * **ما صدر (Ma ṣadr):** "Has not been issued" – a common way to express negative past perfect in Mesopotamian Arabic. * **راح (rāḥ):** Future marker, very prevalent in Iraqi/Mesopotamian dialects. Equivalent to "will" or "going to." More colloquial than سي (say) which is more formal. * **وفقاً لـ (wifqan li-):** “According to” - standard Arabic, understood universally, but frequently used in more educated speech in the region. * **وكالة (wikāla):** “Agency” – standard Arabic, commonly used. * **الزلزال (al-zilzāl):** "The earthquake" - Standard Arabic, widely understood. * **ما وصل قوة (mā waṣal quwwat):** “Did not reach the magnitude/strength of”. This construction is very natural in colloquial Iraqi Arabic.

چا، وِنْفري چانْ دَمُوعْها طايْحة بْوَدَاعْها، لَكِنْ وضحْتْ لْفانْزا إنْها حتِرْجع. (Cha, Winfrey chan damu'ha tayha b-wada'ha, lakin waddaht l-fanza inha hatirja'.)

گوات و جنود أفغانيين دخلوا المنطقة عشان يحمون الموقع و طيارات تحالف ثانية انبعثت تساعد. (Guwat wa junud Afghaniyyin dakhalu al-mintaqa ʿashan yahmun al-mawqiʿ wa ṭayyarat tahaluf thaniya inbaʿthat tusaʿid.)
طاح الطيارة/المروحية فوك بجبال، ويحكون ضرب نار كان السبب. **(Ṭāḥ aṭ-ṭayyāra/al-miḥrūḥiyya fōg bi-jibāl, wa yiḥkūn ḍarb nār kān as-sabab.)** **Breakdown & Linguistic Notes:** * **طاح (Ṭāḥ):** A very common and versatile verb meaning "fell," "crashed," or "went down." More colloquial and common than a more formal verb for "crash." * **الطيارة/المروحية (aṭ-ṭayyāra/al-miḥrūḥiyya):** "The airplane/The helicopter." Using both gives flexibility depending on what *actually* crashed. You'd pick one. * **فوك (Fōg):** "Above," "up high." Standard Mesopotamian Arabic. * **بجبال (bi-jibāl):** "In/with mountains." The "bi-" prefix indicates location. * **ويحكون (wa yiḥkūn):** "And they say," "reportedly," "it's said." A very common way to express belief/reports, softening the statement. Instead of directly saying "it *is* believed..." * **ضرب نار (ḍarb nār):** Literally "hitting of fire," the standard colloquial way to say "gunfire" or "hostile fire." * **كان السبب (kān as-sabab):** "Was the cause." This translation aims for naturalness within a Mesopotamian Arabic dialect, prioritizing common phrasing over literal accuracy. It’s the kind of sentence you’d *hear* in conversation.

.گالوا المنظمة العالمية للصحة و منظمة أطباء بلا حدود و جمعية مانغولا الخيرية إنّها أسوأ وباء سجل بالبلد (pronounced: Galu al-munadhama al-'alamiyya lil-siha wa munadhmat atibba' bila hudud wa jam'iyyat Mangola al-khayriyya innaha aswa' waba' sujjil bil-balad.)
گال المتحدث باسم منظمة أطباء بلا حدود، ريتشارد فيرمان: "أنگولا رايحة صوب أسوأ وباء مرّ عليها، و الوضع لسه سيء كتير بأنگولا"، گال. لكن سوق المستهلك لأجهزة الكمبيوتر المحمولة راح يتغيّر ويتنوّع بشكل جذري بعد ما أخذت شركة أسوس جائزة تايوان للاستدامة سنة 2007 من المعهد التنفيذي لجمهورية الصين. **(Lakin suq al-mustahlik li-ajhizat al-kumbyutar al-mahmula raah yitghayyar wa yitnawwa' bi-shakl jathri ba'd ma akhathit sharikat ASUS ja'izat Taiwan lil-istidama sanat 2007 min al-ma'had al-tanfidhi li-jumhuriyat al-Seen.)** **Notes on choices & why this is "Mesopotamian" rather than a Gulf or Egyptian Arabic:** * **راح (raah):** This future marker is *very* common in Mesopotamian dialects (Iraq, parts of Syria). Other dialects use things like "sa-" or "hasha". * **يتغيّر ويتنوّع (yitghayyar wa yitnawwa'):** The "y-" prefix indicates the imperfective, common in Iraqi and Syrian Arabic for ongoing changes. The verb choice ("yitnawwa'") for "varied" is also more typical of the region. * **أخذت (akhathit):** The verb "to take/receive" used here, while understood elsewhere, is very frequently used in Iraq to mean "was awarded". * **سنة (sanat):** This is the common word for "year" throughout the Levant and Mesopotamia. * **المعهد التنفيذي (al-ma'had al-tanfidhi):** A fairly literal translation of "Executive Yuan," but using vocabulary common to governmental descriptions in Iraq. * **جمهورية الصين (jumhuriyat al-Seen):** Using "al-Seen" (China) rather than a more colloquial term. This translation aims for a natural flow within the linguistic nuances specific to Mesopotamian Arabic, focusing on vocabulary and grammatical structures most prevalent in Iraqi and Syrian dialects.

القصة المِعرضة بالـْأوبرا الفرنسية، للمؤلف كامي سان سانس، هي عن فنان "حياتُه مُتحَكَّمة بـْحُبّه لـْالمُخدرات واليابان". **(al-qissa al-muʿarraḍa bil-ʼūbira al-fransiyya, lil-muʼallif Kami San Sans, hiya ʿan fannan “ḥayātuhu mutaḥakkima bi-ḥubbihi lil-mukhadderat wal-yābān.”)** **Notes on choices reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic (specifically Baghdad/Central dialect influences):** * **المِعرضة (al-muʿarraḍa):** “Presented” - a common way to express “presented” in a storytelling context in Iraqi Arabic. More formal than a simple عرض (ʿarḍ). * **بـْ (bi-):** The "b-" prefix on verbs and nouns indicating "by" or "with" is very characteristic of Mesopotamian Arabic. * **مُتحَكَّمة (mutaḥakkima):** "Dictated/controlled" – A standard Arabic form, but frequently used in this way in Iraqi speech. * **حُبّه (ḥubbihi):** "His love" – standard Arabic grammatical structure. * **المُخدرات (al-mukhadderat):** "Drugs" – a commonly used term. * The quotation marks are maintained for the direct phrase about the artist.

ﮔال بيري انه "يرجع لـ تكساس يقيم نتائج الاجتماع الليلة، ويشوف اذا اكو طريق يمشي بيه بهالسباق"، بس بعدين گال انه راح يبقى بالسباق ويتنافس بانتخابات كارولينا الجنوبية يوم ٢١ جانوري. **(Transliteration: Gal Berry enneh "yirja' li-Texas yqayyim nata'ij al-ijtima' al-leela, wa yshoof itha ako tareeq yimshi beeh bihal-sibaaq," bas ba'dein gal enneh raah yibqa bil-sibaaq wa yitnaafas bi-intikhaabaat Karolina al-Janubi yom 21 Yanwari.)** **Explanation of choices, reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic features:** * **ﮔال (Gal):** Common Mesopotamian Arabic verb for "said." * **انه (Enneh):** "That" - very common connector. * **يرجع (Yirja'):** "He will return" - Using future tense construction common in the dialect. * **يقيم (Yqayyim):** "He assesses/evaluates" - Standard Arabic root, but pronunciation adapts to the dialect. * **نتائج الاجتماع الليلة (Nata'ij al-ijtima' al-leela):** "Results of the meeting tonight" - "Al-ijtima'" for "caucus" since a direct equivalent is less common. * **ويشوف (Wa yshoof):** “And he sees/checks" – Colloquial and common for "determine". * **اكو (Ako):** “There is/are” – very common Mesopotamian Arabic word borrowed from Akkadian. * **طريق يمشي بيه (Tareeq yimshi beeh):** "A path he walks in it" – Literally, but conveys "a path forward." Using "yimshi" (he walks) as a metaphor for proceeding. * **بهالسباق (Bihal-sibaaq):** "In this race" - Colloquial contraction. * **بس (Bas):** "But" - Common connector. * **راح يبقى (Raah yibqa):** "He will remain" - Future tense again. * **يتنافس (Yitnaafas):** “He competes”. * **انتخابات (Intikhaabaat):** “Elections”. * **يوم (Yom):** "Day". * **٢١ (21):** Numbers are generally pronounced as in Standard Arabic. * **جانوري (Yanwari):** "January" - Pronunciation adapted to the dialect. This translation aims for a natural sound in Mesopotamian Arabic, using common vocabulary and grammatical structures while accurately conveying the meaning of the English original. The specific dialect nuances (e.g., from Baghdad, Basra, Mosul) would vary slightly, but this is a broadly understandable version.

المريض چان مودّي النيجرية، وهناك كام حالة من فايروس الإيبولا ظهرت. (al-mareed chan muddi al-nijiriya, wa hunaak kaam ḥaala min vayrus al-ebola ẓahrat.)
المستشفى اتبع الإجراءات اللازمة للسيطرة على العدوى، بما في ذلك عزل المريض عن باقي المرضى لمنع انتقال العدوى اليهم. (Al-mustashfa atba’ al-ijra’at al-lazima lil-saytara ‘ala al-‘adwa, bima fi thalik ‘azl al-mareed ‘an baqi al-marada liman’ intiqal al-‘adwa ilayhim.)
قبل البُرمامج "سيمبسونز"، اشتغل سايمون على عدة برامج بشغلات مختلفة.
.بالثمانينات اشتغل على برامج مثل تاكسي، تشيرز، وبرنامج تريسي أولمان
بـ 1989 ساعد بـ إنشاء مسلسل "ذي سمبسونز" وية بروكس و غرونينغ، و چان مسؤول عن توظيف أول فريق كتابة للمسلسل.

بعدين اجت تقارير گالت الطيارة تلگت تهديد بِنِفْجَار ورجعِت للدَيرة، وهبِطت بـ قندهار. (Ba'deen ajet taqaareer galt el-ṭayyara telget tahdeed bi-nifjaar wa-rja'et lid-deera, wa habtet bi-Qandahar.)
.گالوا التقارير الأولية إن الطيارة رجعت لأفغانستان بعد ما منعوها تهبط اضطراري بمدينة أورومتشي (Galū al-taqārīr al-awwaliyya inn al-ṭayyāra raj'at li-Afghānistān ba'd ma mana'ūhā tahbit iḍṭirārī bi-madīnat Ūrumchi.)

المغني سنجو شارما بدا السهرة، و وراه جاي شانكار شودري. قدموا چبّان بهوج بهجان هم. المغني راجو خاندوال كان يرافقهم.

ميَّة صحن چابّان بوغ كُدِّموا لبابا شَيَّام. (miyya ṣaḥn Chhappan Bhog kuddima libaba Shayyam.) **Explanation of Choices & Linguistic Considerations:** * **ميَّة (miyya):** "108" - Uses the standard Mesopotamian Arabic word for "one hundred" (miyya) with the addition of the quantifier. * **صَحن (ṣaḥn):** "plates" - The most common and understood word for "plate" across Mesopotamian dialects. * **چابّان بوغ (Chhappan Bhog):** Transliterated directly. Given this is a very specific Hindu cultural term, direct transliteration is best, as creating a descriptive Arabic phrase would lose nuance and recognition. It would be understood as a foreign, specific offering. * **كُدِّموا (kuddima):** "were served" - A common and formal verb for "to serve" or "to present" (passive voice construction, common in Arabic). * **لبابا (libaba):** "to Baba" – "li" is the preposition meaning "to" and "baba" is a respectful title akin to "father" or "respected elder", used directly as it appears in the English. * **شَيَّام (Shayyam):** Transliterated directly, keeping the original name. **Important Notes on Mesopotamian Arabic:** * **Dialectal Variation:** Mesopotamian Arabic is *not* a single, unified dialect. There is significant variation between the dialects spoken in Mosul, Baghdad, Basra, etc. This translation aims for a broadly understandable form, leaning towards a more generally understood vocabulary. * **Transliteration:** Transliterating foreign words (like *Chhappan Bhog* and *Baba Shyam*) is essential when there isn't a direct, culturally equivalent Arabic term. * **Formal vs. Colloquial:** I've leaned toward a slightly more formal register ("kuddima" instead of a more colloquial "jaabu" - brought) because of the religious context and the overall tone of the English sentence.
لاكھا سينغ قدم چپن بوگ بھجن همين، والمغني راجو خاندوال كان يرافقونه. (Lakkha Singh qaddam chhappan bhog bhajan haymin, wal-mughanni Raju Khandelwal kan yuraafiqoonah.)

ﮔﺎﻝ رﺋﻴﺲ ﺑﺮﻧﺎﻣﺞ ﻣﻜﻮﻛﺎت ﻧﺎﺳﺎ، ﻧ. واﻳﻦ ﻫﻴﻞ ﺟﻮﻧﻴﻮر، اﻧﻪ ﺍﻟﻔﻮم ﻃﺎﺡ "ﺑﻌﺪ اﻟﻮﻗﺖ اﻟﻠﻲ ﻧﻬﺘﻤﺶ ﺑﻴﻪ". (Gāl rayīs barnāmij makūkāt NASA, N. Wayne Heel Junior, inna al-fūm ṭāḥ "baʿd al-waqt illī nahtammish biih.")
خمس دقايق من بداية العرض، ريح بدت تجيب، تقريبًا دقيقة وحدة بعدها الريح وصلت 70 كيلو بالساعة… بعدين مطر نزل، بس قوي وحجمه جبير بحيث يصفع الجلد مثل الإبرة، بعدين برد نزل من السما، الناس خافوا وصاروا يصرخون ويدوسون على بعض.
ضاعت اختي وصديقتها، وبلتالي چنت رايح شفت اثنين معاقين على الكراسي، الناس بس تتخطى وادفعهم، هيچ هي السالفة، كال ارماند فرساجي. **(Pronunciation guide - approximate, as dialects vary greatly):** * **ḍāʿat** (dah-ʿat) - lost * **ʾukhti** (ukh-tee) - my sister * **wa ṣadīqat-ha** (wa sah-dee-qat-ha) - and her friend * **wa bil-tālī** (wa bil-taa-lee) - and consequently / on my way * **kunt rāyiḥ** (kunt raa-yehh) - I was going * **shuft itnayn muʿāqīn** (shuft it-nayn moo-aa-qeen) - I saw two disabled people * **ʿala l-karāsī** (ʿala l-ka-raa-see) - on wheelchairs * **al-nās bas titkhatta wa tdaffuhum** (al-naas bas tit-khah-tah wa tdaffu-hum) - people just jump over and push them * **heej hey al-sālfah** (heej hey al-saal-fah) - that's the story / that's how it was * **kāl Armand Versace** (kaal Ar-mand Ver-sa-chee) - Armand Versace said. **Important Notes:** * This is a general translation aiming for a common, understood form of Mesopotamian Arabic. Specific vocabulary and phrasing will vary considerably between cities (Baghdad, Basra, Mosul, etc.) and even neighborhoods. * The phrase “disabled people” is translated as “muʿāqīn” which is a standard term, but sensitivity regarding terminology is important. * The "hey" at the end is common in Iraqi Arabic to reinforce a point or describe a situation. * The use of "bil-tālī" is a bit more formal but conveys the sequence of events ("and on my way…") well.
.كالNHK هم خبروا إن محطة كاشيوازاكي كاريوا للطاقة النووية بمحافظة نيغاتا تشتغل طبيعي.

چانَ شوية طرق اتخربت، وخدمة السكة الحديد انقطعت بالمنطقة المتضررة، ومطار نوتو بمحافظة إيشيكاوا لسه مقفول.

ﺷﺎﻓﻮ ﺍﻟﺒﺎﺣﺜﻴﻦ ﺑﻠﻮﺭﺍﺕ ﺗﺸﻜّﻠﺖ ﺑﺒﻮﻝ ﺍﻟﻘﻄﻂ ﺑﺴﺒﺐ ﺿﻴﻔﺔ ﻣﻴﻼﻣﻴﻦ ﻭ ﺳﻴﺎﻧﻮﺭﻳﻚ ﺍﺳﻴﺪ.

چـتـّـه ثمانين بالمية من بضاعتـنه تخـرّج ضـريـب بالدول الـوسطى بامريكا الـجنوبية. نـدلـّـلـك. **(Chittah thamanin bil-miyya min buḍaʿatina tikhraj ḍarīb bil-duwal al-wusta bi-Amrika al-Janūbiya. N-dallilak.)** **Explanation of choices & linguistic considerations:** * **"Yet"**: The nuance of "yet" is often conveyed through context in Mesopotamian Arabic. I've implied it with the flow of the sentence. * **"Eighty percent"**: "ثمانين بالمية" (thamanin bil-miyya) is the standard way to say eighty percent. * **"Goods"**: "بضاعتـنه" (buḍaʿatina) means "our goods" (with the possessive suffix). * **"Were taxed"**: "تخـرّج ضـريـب" (tikhraj ḍarīb) literally "exits/is taken as tax". This is a very common way to express being taxed in the dialect. Using a passive form directly like "were taxed" isn't natural. * **"Tariffs"**: "ضـريـب" (ḍarīb) covers both taxes and tariffs. The context clarifies it refers to taxes *on* goods. * **"Central American countries"**: "الدول الـوسطى بامريكا الـجنوبية" (al-duwal al-wusta bi-Amrika al-Janūbiya) - "al-duwal" (the countries), "al-wusta" (the central/middle), "bi-Amrika al-Janūbiya" (in South America - commonly used to refer to Central America as well, as the distinction isn't always strongly made in colloquial speech). * **"We treat you"**: "نـدلـّـلـك" (N-dallilak) - This is *the* standard, most natural way to say "we treat you well" or "we pamper you" in Mesopotamian Arabic. It conveys a sense of hospitality and kindness. A more literal translation wouldn't feel idiomatic. The "N-" prefix is the "we" conjugation. "-ak" is the "you" suffix. **Important Note:** Mesopotamian Arabic is a *continuum* of dialects. This translation aims for a generally understandable form, leaning towards the Baghdad/central Iraq area, but elements could vary depending on the specific town or city.

هونه استقال، و راح ينصّبوا مكانه إد ديفي عضو البرلمان. نورمان لامب عضو البرلمان هم متوقع ياخذ منصب وزير التجارة اللي ديفي خلاه. **(Huna istāqāl, wa rāḥ yinṣṣabu makānahu Īd Dīvī ‘uḍw al-barmān. Nūrmān Lāmb ‘uḍw al-barmān ham mitawaqqa‘ yākhudh manṣib wazīr al-tijāra illī Dīvī khallāh.)** **Notes on choices & why this is "Mesopotamian" Arabic:** * **هونه (Huna):** This is a common pronunciation of "Huhne" that fits the Mesopotamian dialect. * **استقال (istāqāl):** Standard Arabic verb for "resigned," widely understood and used in Mesopotamian Arabic. * **راح ينصّبوا (rāḥ yinṣṣabu):** "They will install/appoint" - uses the common future construction with *rāḥ* + present tense. The form *yinṣṣabu* is preferred over more formal constructions in colloquial speech. This construction is characteristic of Iraqi and broader Mesopotamian dialects. * **مكانه (makānahu):** "In his place" - standard. * **إد ديفي (Īd Dīvī):** Transliteration of "Ed Davey." * **عضو البرلمان (‘uḍw al-barmān):** "Member of Parliament." This is the standard way to say "MP" and is used across Arabic dialects. * **نورمان لامب (Nūrmān Lāmb):** Transliteration of "Norman Lamb." * **هم (ham):** “Also/too.” Commonly used in Mesopotamian Arabic. * **متوقع (mitawaqqa‘):** "Expected" - standard Arabic. * **يأخذ (yākhudh):** "To take" - standard Arabic. * **منصب وزير التجارة (manṣib wazīr al-tijāra):** “The position of Minister of Commerce/Trade.” * **اللي (illī):** The relative pronoun “that/which.” Extremely common in colloquial Arabic, and specifically very prevalent in Mesopotamian dialects. * **خلاه (khallāh):** "He left it/vacated it." Using *khallāh* in this context is a very natural way to express "vacating" a position in colloquial Mesopotamian Arabic. This translation aims for natural-sounding colloquial speech typical of Iraq and surrounding areas, avoiding excessively formal phrasing. It prioritizes readability and understanding for speakers of Mesopotamian Arabic.
هونه وبريس مَوعدهم يِظهرون بِمحكمة وستمنستر يوم ١٦ شباط. (Hūnah wa Brīs mawʿidhum yidhharūn bi-maḥkamat Westminster yōm sittataʿash shubāṭ.)
راحوا ضحية كل من نيكولاس الدن، عمره ٢٥ سنة، و زاكاري كدّيباك، عمره ٢١ سنة. كدّيباك كان السايق.
إدغار فيغيلا أِصيب بجروح في ذراعه وفكه، بينما كريستوفر شنايدر ظل محتاج لعملية تجميلية لوجهه. **(ʾIdġār Vīgīllā ʾiṣīb bi-jrūḥ fī ḏrāʿihī wa fakihī, baynamā Krīstōfir Shnāydir ẓalla muḥtāj li-ʿamaliyyah tajmīliyyah li-wajhih.)** **Notes on choices reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic (specifically Baghdad/Central dialects):** * **أصيب (ʾiṣīb)** - "was injured/received wounds" - a common verb for injury. * **جروح (jrūḥ)** - “wounds” * **ذراعه وفكه (ḏrāʿihī wa fakihī)** - "his arm and his jaw" - using the attached pronoun suffix (ـه) is very common. * **بينما (baynamā)** - “while” - a standard conjunction. * **ظل محتاج (ẓalla muḥtāj)** - “remained needing/was left requiring” - a natural phrasing. * **تجميلية (tajmīliyyah)** - “reconstructive/cosmetic” - widely used for surgical reconstruction. * **لوجهه (li-wajhih)** - “for his face”.
سلاح اوكا خَرِبْ بينما كانْ مُوَجَّهْ لرأسْ رَجَلْ خامِس. شنايدر عندَه وَجَعْ مُستَمِرّ، عَمَى بعين وحدة، قطعة مْن جمجمته مَش موجودة، ووَجهه مْعْمُول مِن تيتانيوم.
شْنيدرْ شَهَدْ عَنْ طَرِيقْ الفيديُو مِن قَاعِدَةْ جُوّيّةْ أمْرِيكِيّةْ بِبِلَادُه.
و ورا فعالية الأربعاء، كاربانيدو تنافس في سباقين فرديين بالبطولة.
اول سباق الها چانت سلاлом، و أجت ما كملت في جولتها الأولى. 36 من الـ 116 متسابق نفس النتيجة چان الهم بهالسباق. **(Pronunciation guide for those unfamiliar: awwal sibaag alha kaanat slaalom, wa ajet ma kamalat fi jawlitha al-oola. Sittah wa thalathoon min al-mi’ah wa sittah ‘ashar mutasaabiq nafs an-natija kaan hum bihal-sibaag.)** **Explanation of choices & linguistic notes, for context as a linguist (not part of the returned sentence):** * **"Her first was..." (اول سباق الها چانت...)**: Using "awwal sibaag alha" (first race of her) is a natural way to express this. "Chant" is the common verb "to be" in Mesopotamian Arabic. * **"Slalom" (سلاлом)**: Transliterated as it's a loanword. * **"Did Not Finish" (ما كملت)**: The most common and understandable way to convey this is "ma kamalat" (did not complete). * **"run" (جولتها الأولى)**: "Jawlitha al-oola" (her first round/lap). Using "jawla" is standard for a race run. * **"competitors" (متسابق)**: "Mutasaabiq" is the standard word for competitor. * **"same result" (نفس النتيجة)**: "Nafs an-natija" is directly equivalent. * **"in that race" (بهالسباق)**: "Bi-hal sibaag" (in this race) is conversational and natural. * **Numbers (36 of 116):** I used standard Arabic numerals and the constructions “Sittah wa thalathoon min al-mi’ah wa sittah ‘ashar.” * **Dialectal Features:** The use of "چ" (pronounced like "ch" in church) for the "sh" sound is a key feature of many Mesopotamian Arabic dialects, particularly those in Baghdad and surrounding areas. The use of the verb “ajat” (came) instead of “kaanat” to express “was” is also prevalent.
سباقها الثاني، السلالوم العملاق، شافت فيه تكمل بالعاشر بالجموعة النسائية للجالسين، بوقت مجمل ٤:٤١.٣٠، أبطأ من الفائزة الأولى النمساوية كلوديا لوش بـ ٢:١١.٦٠ دقيقة، و أبطأ من صاحبة المركز التاسع المجرية جيونغي داني بـ ١:٠٩.٠٢ دقيقة.
أربعة متزلجات من مجموعة الجلوس النسائية ما كملن مساراتهن، و ٤٥ من الـ ١١٧ متزلج total اللي في سباق السلالوم العملاق ما اجو ترتيب بالسباق. (ʾarbaʿa mutazallijāt min majmūʿat al-julūs al-nisāʾiyya mā kammaln masārātihinna, wa ʾarbaʿa wa-khamsūn min al-miʾa wa-sabʿat ʿashar mutazallij total illi fi sibāq al-salālūm al-ʿimlāq mā jū trtīb bil-sibāq.)
انضباط الشرطة في ماديا براديش استرجعت اللابتوب وال موبايل المسروقين. (ʾinḍibāṭ al-šurṭa fī mādiyā brādish ʾistrajʿat al-lābtūb wal-mūbāʾil al-masrūqayn.)
گال معاون مدير عام الشرطة دي كي آريا، " قبضنا على خمسة أشخاص اعتدوا على المرأة السويسرية واسترجعنا موبايلها ولابتوبها."
المتهمون هم بابا كنجار، بوثا كنجار، رامبرو كنجار، كازا كنجار، وفيشنو كنجار.
ﮔﺎﻝ ﻣُﺪﻳﺮ ﺷُرﻃﺔ ﭼﻨﺪﺭﺍ ﺷﻴﮑﺎﺭ ﺳﻮﻻﻧﮕﻲ ﺇﻧّﻪ ﺍﻟﻤﺘﻬﻤﻴﻦ ﻇﻬﺮﻭ ﺑﺎﻟﻤﺤﻜﻤﺔ ﻭﻭﺟﻮﻫﻬﻢ ﻣﻐﻄّﺎﺓ. (Gāl mudīr shurṭa Chandra Shīkār Sūlāngī ʾinn-i al-mutahhamīn ẓharū bil-maḥkama wujūhihim mughaṭṭāyah.)
چا، ثلثة ناس چانوا جوه بيت من سيارة ضربتة، ولا واحد منهم انصاب. **(cha, thlatha nas thanu juwah bayt min sayyara dhrabat, wala wahed minhum insab.)** **Explanation of choices & nuances for a linguist:** * **چا (cha):** This is a very common discourse marker in Mesopotamian Arabic (especially Central/Southern dialects) functioning like "though," "although," or "well..." to introduce a contrast. It's far more natural than trying a direct equivalent of "although" using a complex conjunction. * **ثلثة (thlatha):** Standard Arabic number, widely used. * **ناس (nas):** “People,” a very common word. * **چانوا (thanu):** Imperfective past of "to be" – "they were." This is the common form for narrating past events. * **جوه (juwah):** "Inside" - a very common colloquial term. * **بيت (bayt):** "House" - standard. * **من سيارة ضربتة (min sayyara dhrabat):** "By a car that hit it." The use of *min* (by) with the verb directly following is typical structure. The suffix –تة (-ta) on *dhrabat* (hit) indicates the house is the object. * **ولا واحد منهم (wala wahed minhum):** "Not one of them." *Wala* is the negative *wa* (and). * **انصاب (insab):** “Was injured.” This verb carries the meaning of being harmed/injured. It's preferable to direct translations of "hurt" that might sound overly formal. **Important Note:** Mesopotamian Arabic is a dialect *continuum*. This translation is geared toward a Central Iraqi (Baghdad area) dialect. Dialectal variations would exist; for example, in more Southern areas, you'd hear slightly different vocabulary choices.
لكن السايق تجرّح بشكل خطير براسه. (Lakin al-saa’iq tjarrah bishakl khateer bira’su.)
الطريق اللي صار بيّها التصادم انغلق مؤقتًا لحد ما الدفاع المدني طلّع السايق من الأودي تي تي الحمرا.

بعدين نُقل لـ مستشفى أدنبروك في كامبريدج.

چاﯧﺶ ﺑﺎﻣﻴﻼ ﻓﻴﺮﮔﺴﻮﻥ ﻣﻦ ﺟﺎﻣﻌﺔ ﺩﻧﺪﻱ ﺩﻳﮕﻮﻝ، "ﺻﺤﻔﻴﻴﻦ ﯠﻛﺄﻧﻬﻢ ﻳﻤﺸﻮﻥ ﻋﻠﻰ ﺣﺒﻞ ﻣﺶ ﺁﻣﻦ ﻟﻤﺎ ﻳﻨﺸﺮﻭﻥ ﺻﻮﺭ ﻭ ﺷﻲ ﻣﻦ ﻣﺘﻬﻤﻴﻦ." (Cha'ish Bamila Firguson min Jami'at Dundee digool, "Sahfiyyeen w ka'enhum yimshoon 'ala habl mish aamen lama yinshroon suwar wa shi min mutahammeen.")
مكتب المدعي العام، اللي مسؤول بشكل كامل عن الملاحقات القضائية، أشار للصحفيين ما راح يعلقون أكثر لين ما يصير قرار بالإدانة. (Maktab al-mudda'i al-'aam, illi mas'ool bishakl kaamil 'an al-mulaahaqaat al-qadaa'iyya, ashaar lil-sahafiyyeen ma raah ya'allaqoon akthar leen ma yseer qaraar bil-idaana.)
الوثيقة، حسب التسريب، راح تتطرق للنزاع على الحدود، اللي فلسطين تدّعي حقها فيها على أساس حدود قبل حرب الستة وستين في الشرق الأوسط.
مواضيع تانية اللي اتغطّت، كأنّه، مستقبل حال القدس، اللي مقدّسة لبدو الدولتين، و مسألة وادي الأردن.
إسرائيل تطالب بوجود عسكري مستمر بالوادي لمدة عشر سنين بعد ما يتوقع اتفاق، بينما السلطة الفلسطينية توافق على هالوجود بس لمدة خمس سنين.
كال اللي يرمون في تجربة مكافحة الآفات الإضافية لازم يكونون تحت إشراف صارم من الحراس، لأن التجربة كانت مراقبة وفعاليتها متقيّمة.
بشراكة بين دائرة المتنزهات والحياة البرية (NPWS) وجمعية الرماة الرياضيين الأستراليين (فرع نيو ساوث ويلز) Inc، تم تجنيد متطوعين مؤهلين، ضمن برنامج الصيد التابع لجمعية الرماة الرياضيين. (bisharakah bain da'irat al-mutanazzahat wal-hayat al-barriyah (NPWS) wa jam'iyyat al-rumat al-riyadiyyin al-ustraliyyin (far' niw south wailz) Inc, tam tajnid mutatawwi'in mu'ahhalin, ضمن barnamaj al-said al-tabi' li-jam'iyyat al-rumat al-riyadiyyin.)
وِگال ميك أوفلاين، المدير المساعد لشؤون المحافظة على المتنزهات والتراث بالـ NPWS، أربعَة صيّادين إنتخبوا للعمليّة الأولى للصيد، أخذوا تعليمات شاملة عن السلامة والتدريب. **(Wi-gal Meek O’Flynn, al-mudeer al-musa’id li-shu’oon al-muhaafaza ‘ala al-mutanazzahaat wal-turaath bil-NPWS, arba’a sayyaadeen intakhbu lil-‘amaliyya al-oola lil-sayd, akhadhoo ta’leemaat shaamila ‘an al-salaama wal-tadreeb.)** **Note:** This is a fairly formal rendering, aiming for accuracy given the official context of the English sentence. Dialectal variations *within* Mesopotamian Arabic are significant, but this is a generally understandable version across the region (Southern and Central Iraq, parts of Syria, and the Turkish/Iranian borders). I have tried to balance modern standard Arabic influences (common in official speech) with genuine colloquial usage. Also, I've retained "NPWS" as it is likely an acronym commonly used even *within* Arabic-speaking contexts related to that organization. I chose "صيادين" (sayyaadeen) for shooters, as it accurately conveys "hunters" which is the closest equivalent in this context.
مارْتَيلي حَلَّف مجلسًا انتخابيًا مؤقتًا جديدًا (سي إي بي) مؤلفًا من تسعة أعضاء أمس.
هَذَا خُمُس دورة تطوير مهني لمارتيلي خلال أربع سنين.
الشهر اللي فات، لجنة رئاسية نصت على استقالة الرئيس التنفيذي السابق كجزء من مجموعة إجراءات عشان نوجه البلد نحو انتخابات جديدة.
كانت اللجنة ردّ فعل مارتيلي على الاحتجاجات الواسعة ضدّ الحكومة اللي بدت في شهر تشرين الأول.
الاحتجاجات العنيفة أحيانًا اندلعت بسبب ما حصل من تأخير بالانتخابات، وبعضها متأخر من سنة ٢٠١١.
حوالي الستين حالة من آي بودات الخربانة اللي تسخّن واجد، اتّروى، وسبّبت ست حرائق، وخَلّت أربعة ناس بحروق بسيطة. **(Ḥawālī al-sittīn ḥālah min āy būdāt al-kharbānah illi tissakhkhan wājid, ittarwa, wa sabbabat sitt ḥarā’iq, wa khallat arba’ah nās bi-ḥuruq basīṭah.)** **Explanation of choices & linguistic considerations:** * **"Around 60"**: "حوالي الستين" (Ḥawālī al-sittīn) – Standard way to express "around sixty." * **"cases of malfunctioning iPods"**: "حالة من آي بودات الخربانة" (ḥālah min āy būdāt al-kharbānah) - "ḥālah" (case) , "āy būdāt" (iPods – adapted transliteration), "al-kharbānah" (broken/malfunctioning - feminine plural to agree with "āy būdāt"). * **"overheating"**: "اللي تسخّن واجد" (illi tissakhkhan wājid) - "illi" (that/which) connects it to the iPods, "tissakhkhan" (it heats up - present tense conveys ongoing action of overheating), "wājid" (a lot/very). This is a very common colloquial way to express overheating. * **"have been reported"**: "اتّروى" (ittarwa) – Passive form, meaning “were reported”. Commonly used in spoken Mesopotamian Arabic for news/reports. * **"causing"**: "وسبّبت" (wa sabbabat) – "wa" (and), "sabbabat" (caused - feminine singular, agreeing with the implied subject “the overheating"). * **"a total of six fires"**: "ست حرائق" (sitt ḥarā’iq) – "sitt" (six), "ḥarā’iq" (fires - plural). * **"leaving four people"**: "وخلّت أربعة ناس" (wa khallat arba’ah nās) - "wa" (and), "khallat" (left – caused to remain/resulted in), "arba’ah" (four), "nās" (people). * **"with minor burns"**: "بحروق بسيطة" (bi-ḥuruq basīṭah) – “bi-” (with), "ḥuruq" (burns - plural), "basīṭah" (minor/simple - feminine singular, agreeing with "ḥuruq"). **Dialectal Notes:** This translation leans towards a Central Iraqi (Baghdadi) dialect, which is a common baseline for “Mesopotamian Arabic” when a single variant is needed. Variations would exist depending on the specific region (Mosul, Basra, etc.). The goal is to provide a broadly understandable and natural-sounding translation.
گالوا وزارة الاقتصاد والتجارة والصناعة اليابانية (ميـتي) إنهم چانوا يعلمون بـ ٢٧ حادثة مرتبطة بالأجهزة. **(Pronunciation guide for those unfamiliar: Galu wizārat al-iqtisād wa-t-tijāra wa-ṣ-ṣināʿa al-yābāniyya (Mīti) innahum kānū yaʿlamūn bi-sitt wa-ʿishrīn ḥāditha murtabiṭa bi-l-ajhiza.)**
الأسبوع اللي فات، أعلنت وزارة الاقتصاد والتجارة والصناعة (METI) إن شركة آبل خبرتها عن ٣٤ حالة زيادة حرارة زيادة، الشركة سمتها "غير خطيرة". (Al-usbu’ al-li fat, a’lanat wizārat al-iqtisād wal-tijārah wal-sinā’ah (METI) in sharakat Ābl khabarthā ‘an thalāth wa thalāthīn ḥālah ziyādat ḥarārah ziyādah, al-sharikah sammathā “ghair khaṭīrah”.)
الوزارة ردّت بوصف تأجيل آبل للتقرير بـ "مؤسف جداً." (Al-wizārah raddat bi-wasf ta’jīl Ābl lil-taqrīr bi “mū’sif jiddan.”)
زلزال ضرب ماريانا الساعة سبعة تسعة عشرة صباحًا بالتوقيت المحلي (التاسعة تسعة عشرة مساءً بتوقيت جرينتش يوم الجمعة). **(Zilzal ḍaraba Mariyana al-sa'a sab'a tis'ata 'ashra ṣabāḥan bi-t-tawqīt al-maḥallī (at-tāsi'a tis'ata 'ashra masā'an bi-tawqīt Grīniṭš yawm al-jum'a).)**
مكتب إدارة الطوارئ في جزر ماريانا الشمالية گال ماكو أي ضرر اندكّرت بالبلد. **(Maktab idarat al-ṭawāri' fi juzur Mariyana al-Shamaliyya gal ma-ko ay ḍarar indakkarat bil-balad.)** **Explanation of choices & nuances for a Mesopotamian Arabic (specifically Iraqi) flavour:** * **مكتب إدارة الطوارئ (Maktab idarat al-ṭawāri'):** "Office of Emergency Management" - Standard and commonly used phrasing. * **جزر ماريانا الشمالية (Juzur Mariyana al-Shamaliyya):** "Northern Mariana Islands" - Direct transliteration/translation. * **گال (Gal):** This is a very common Iraqi Arabic verb for “said”. Using قال (qaal) is understood, but گال feels more natural in everyday speech. * **ماكو (Ma-ko):** The quintessential Iraqi Arabic negation "there isn't/aren’t." Crucially different from لا (laa) which is more formal. * **أي ضرر (Ay ḍarar):** "Any damage" - Direct translation. * **اندكّرت (Indakkarat):** This means "were reported". It’s a verb commonly used in Iraqi Arabic to indicate something has been mentioned or noted. * **بالبلد (Bil-balad):** "In the country/nation".
همَّ هم مركز التحذير من التسونامي في المحيط الهادي گال ماكو أي علامة على تسونامي. (Hemma hem markaz al-tahdheer min al-tsunami fi al-muheet al-haadi gal maku ay ‘alaamah ‘ala tsunami.)
واحد شرطي فلبيني قديم اخَذْ سياح هونكونغ رهائن عن طريق اختطاف باصهم في مانيلا، عاصمة الفلبين.

سِتَّة رَهائن، بيهم الجهال والشيوخ، انحرّرو باچر، و چِنهُم المصوّرين الفلبينيين.
اكو مصورين اجو مكان الست العجوز چا هي تحتاج الحمام. مِندوزا انضرب بالگوه. (ʾaku muṣawwirīn ʾaju makān il-sit il-ʿajūz ča hi tiḥtāj il-ḥammām. Mindūza inḍrab bil-gūh.) **Explanation of choices & nuances for a Mesopotamian Arabic speaker (specifically Baghdad/Central Iraq dialect):** * **" اكو " (ʾaku)** - This is a very common way to start a sentence meaning "There are" or "So," functioning as a discourse marker. It's natural in spoken Iraqi Arabic. * **"مصورين" (muṣawwirīn)** – Plural of “photographer”. * **"اجو" (ʾaju)** – Means “came” or “took the place of” in this context, commonly used for replacing someone. * **"مكان" (makān)** – "Place of" * **"الست" (il-sit)** – “The lady” – very respectful way of addressing a woman. * **"العجوز" (il-ʿajūz)** – "The old woman/aged lady". * **"چا" (ča)** – Meaning "because/since/as" - very common conjunction in Iraqi Arabic. * **"هي" (hi)** – "She". * **"تحتاج" (tiḥtāj)** – "She needs". * **"الحمام" (il-ḥammām)** – “The lavatory/bathroom.” * **"مِندوزا" (Mindūza)** - Transliterated name. * **"انضرب" (inḍrab)** – “Was hit/shot/gunned down”. The passive voice is preferred in describing such events in Arabic. * **"بالگوه" (bil-gūh)** – Literally "with the bullet". This is a very common, almost idiomatic, way to say "was shot" in Iraqi Arabic. More formal phrasing exists, but this is what a typical Iraqi speaker would use. **Important Notes for a Linguist:** * **Dialectal Variation:** Mesopotamian Arabic is *highly* dialectal. This translation leans heavily towards the Baghdad/Central Iraq dialect. Variations in pronunciation and vocabulary would occur moving north, south, or east within the region. * **Spoken vs. Formal:** This is a translation that prioritizes *natural spoken language*. A more formal translation would use different vocabulary and sentence structures. * **Cultural Context:** The phrasing around "being gunned down" is intentionally direct and reflects how such news is often communicated in the region. There's less emphasis on euphemisms. * **Transliteration:** I've used a fairly standard transliteration scheme. There are always multiple valid ways to transliterate Arabic.

ﮔﺎﻝ ﺗﻮﻣﻲ درﯾﻤﺮ "ﻟﻮﻧﺎ ﭼﺎﻧﺖ أول مَلﮕﻪ ﻟﻠإﻛﺴﺘﺮﯾﻢ. مﺪﯾﺮﻱ الأول. ﻟﻮﻧﺎ ﺗﻮﻓﺖ ﺑﻠﻴﻠﺔ ﮔﻤﺮﻳﻦ. ﺷﻲ ﻧﺎﺩﺭ ﻣﺜﻞﻫﺎ. ﺑﻨﻴﻪ ﻗﻮﯾﺔ." **(Gāl Tōmī Drīmer "Lūnā chānt awwal malga lil-ikstrīm. Mudīrī awwal. Lūnā tūfat bi-līlet gamrayn. Shay nādir mithlahā. Binya gwayya.")** **Notes on choices made for authenticity:** * **ﮔﺎﻝ (Gāl)** - "Said" - A very common and natural way to start a quoted statement in Mesopotamian Arabic. * **ﭼﺎﻧﺖ (Chānt)** – "Was" – More colloquial than كانت (kānat) and typical of the dialect. * **ﻣﻠﮕﻪ (Malga)** – "Queen" – Directly transliterated and understood. * **ﻟﻠإﻛﺴﺘﺮﯾﻢ (Lil-ikstrīm)** - "For the extreme" - Transliteration of "Extreme" as it's a foreign concept and widely used that way. * **ﻣﺪﯾﺮﻱ (Mudīrī)** - "My manager" - Using the possessive pronoun suffix for "my". * **ﺗﻮﻓﺖ (Tūfat)** – "Passed away" – A respectful and common way to say someone died. * **ﺑﻠﻴﻠﺔ (Bi-līlet)** – "On the night of". * **ﮔﻤﺮﻳﻦ (Gamrayn)** – "Two moons". * **ﺷﻲ ﻧﺎﺩﺭ (Shay nādir)** – "Something rare/unique". * **ﻣﺜﻞﻫﺎ (Mithlahā)** – "Like her". * **ﺑﻨﻴﻪ ﻗﻮﯾﺔ (Binya gwayya)** – "Strong woman". "Binya" is specifically "woman" and "gwayya" is "strong" in a very common Mesopotamian Arabic pronunciation.
دوستين "جولددست" رونيلز گال "لونا چانت غريبة گدش مني...يمكن حتى أكثر...احبها و راح اشتاقلها...انشاء الله هي بمكان أحسن." **(Dustin "Golddust" Runnels gal "Luna chant ghareeba gaddesh minni...yemkin hatta akthar...ahibha wa rah ashtagalha...inshallah hi bi makan ahsan.")** **Breakdown of choices & linguistic notes, for context (not part of the requested output):** * **"Gal" (گال)** - Common Mesopotamian Arabic way to say "said" - more colloquial than formal Arabic equivalents. * **"Chant" (چانت)** – Mesopotamian Arabic for "was," a common colloquial form. * **"Ghareeba" (غريبة)** - “Freaky” translated as strange or odd; “freaky” carries connotations not easily directly mapped to a single word. Using “ghareeba” captures the sense of unusualness. * **"Gaddesh" (گدش)** - A very common Mesopotamian Arabic intensifier - "very" or "so." It significantly emphasizes "strange." * **"Minni" (مني)** - "Than me." * **"Yemkin" (يمكن)** – “Maybe” or “possibly.” * **"Hatta Akthar" (حتى أكثر)** – "Even more." * **"Ahibha" (احبها)** – “I love her.” * **"Rah Ashtagalha" (راح اشتاقلها)** - This is the most natural way to express "I will miss her" in Mesopotamian Arabic. "Ashtagal" is the verb for missing someone, and the "rah" prefix indicates future tense. * **"Inshallah" (انشاء الله)** – "Hopefully" or "God willing" - extremely common in everyday speech. * **"Hi" (هي)** - "She." * **"Bi Makan Ahsan" (بمكان أحسن)** – “In a better place." I aimed for a translation that feels natural and would be readily understood by a speaker of Mesopotamian Arabic, prioritizing colloquialisms over strictly formal Arabic. This takes into account the emotional weight and informal tone of the original quote.
من بين 1400 شخص استُطلعت آراؤهم قبل الانتخابات الفيدرالية لسنة 2010، زادت نسبة المعارضين لتحويل أستراليا إلى جمهورية بنسبة 8 بالمية من سنة 2008.
.گالت رئيسة الوزراء بالوكالة جوليا جيلارد خلال حملة الانتخابات الفيدرالية عام 2010 إنها تعتقد أن أستراليا لازم تصير جمهورية بعد ما تخلص فترة حكم الملكة إليزابيث الثانية. (Gālat ra'īs al-wuzarā' bil-wikāla Jūlyā Jīllārd khilāl ḥamlat al-intikhābāt al-fidrāliyya 'ām 2010 innahā ta'taqid inn Austrālyā lāzim tsīr jumhūriyya ba'd mā tkhallas fatrat ḥukm al-malika Īlīzābīt al-thāniyya.)
٣٤ بالمية من اللي استطلعت رأيهم بالاستطلاع، وياكلون هالرأي، ويريدون الملكة إليزابيث الثانية تكون آخر ملكة لأستراليا.
بِـ أطراف الإستطلاع، 29 بالمية من اللي انستطلعوا رأيهم يخابرون أستراليا لازم تصير جمهورية بأقرب وقت، بينما 31 بالمية يخابرون أستراليا ما لازم تصير جمهورية أبدًا.

كوومو، ابن تلاثة وخمسين سنة، بدا حكمه في بداية هالسنة ووقّع قانون بالشهر الماضي يمشي زواج المثليين. **(Kuūmō, ibn tilāth wa khamsīn sana, bada ḥukmuh fi bidāyat hal-sana wa waqqaʿ qānūn bil-shahr al-māḍī yimshi zawāj al-mithliyyīn.)** **Explanation of choices reflecting Mesopotamian Arabic features:** * **كوومو (Kuūmō):** Transliteration of the name, common practice. * **ابن تلاثة وخمسين سنة (Ibn tilāth wa khamsīn sana):** "Son of three and fifty years" is a very common way to state age in Mesopotamian Arabic, more natural than directly saying "aged 53." * **بدا حكمه (Bada ḥukmuh):** "His rule began" – a natural way to express the start of a governorship. * **في بداية هالسنة (Fi bidāyat hal-sana):** "At the beginning of *this* year." The use of "hal-" (هال-) is a very distinct Mesopotamian feature for demonstrative pronouns ("this"). * **وقّع قانون (Waqqaʿ qānūn):** "He signed a law." Standard. * **بالشهر الماضي (Bil-shahr al-māḍī):** "In the past month." Standard. * **يمشي زواج المثليين (Yimshi zawāj al-mithliyyīn):** "Makes same-sex marriage work/allowed/legal." "Yimshi" is incredibly common in Iraqi/Mesopotamian Arabic to indicate something being permitted, functional, or in effect. Using a verb like “legalize” directly can sound overly formal.
ﮔﺎﻝ ﻫَﺬَا ﮔَﻠﺎﻡ ﻧَﺎﺱ ﻭ ﻫُﻤَﺎﻳَﺔ. (Gal hatha glam nas wa humaya.) **(Alternative, slightly more formal/literary):** ﮔﺎﻝ ﻫَﺬﺍ ﻫُﻮ ﺣَﺪﻳﺚ ﺳﻴﺎﺳﻲ ﻭ ﺗَﻔَﺎﻫَﺔ. (Gal hatha huw hadith siyasi wa tafaha.) **Explanation of choices & linguistic considerations:** * **"Referred to"**: The most natural way to convey "referred to" in this context is simply using "ﮔﺎﻝ" (gal - he said). Mesopotamian Arabic often omits relative pronouns/verbs in such constructions. * **"Rumors"**: "ﮔَﻠﺎﻡ ﻧَﺎﺱ" (glam nas) – literally "talk of people" – is a very common and idiomatic way to refer to rumors, gossip, or hearsay. It captures the informal nature of the original. "ﻫُﻮ ﺣَﺪﻳﺚ" (huw hadith - it is talk) is also correct, but leans more formal. * **"Political chatter"**: "ﺣَﺪﻳﺚ ﺳﻴﺎﺳﻲ" (hadith siyasi) - "political talk/discourse" is a direct translation and works well, especially in the second, more formal version. The first version uses the broader "glam nas" to implicitly cover this aspect. * **"Silliness"**: "ﻫُﻤَﺎﻳَﺔ" (humaya) is a common colloquial term for "silliness," "nonsense," or "triviality" in many Mesopotamian dialects. "ﺗَﻔَﺎﻫَﺔ" (tafaha) is a more standard Arabic word for "triviality" or "frivolity" and is suitable for a more formal register. * **Dialectal variations**: Mesopotamian Arabic isn't a single unified dialect. I've aimed for a broadly understandable version that would be comprehensible across a wide range of regions within Iraq and surrounding areas.

يكدر ينسحب خفيف حيّل، ويلصك على معدن ثاني. يكدر ينسحب حيل خفيف بحيث چانوا يستخدموهsometimes يزخرفون الصور المرسومة بالإيد بالكتب المسمّاة "المنشورات المضيئة". **(Pronunciation Guide - approximate, dialect varies greatly even *within* Mesopotamia):** * **Yikdar** (يكدر) - It can * **Yinsahab** (ينسحب) - Be drawn/pulled/made thin * **Khifeef** (خفيف) - Thin * **Heel** (حيّل) - Very * **Wyalssik** (ويلصك) - And stick * **'ala** (على) - On * **Ma'dan** (معدن) - Metal * **Thani** (ثاني) - Other/Second * **Heel** (حيل) - Very (repeated for emphasis) * **Bihayt** (بحيث) - So that/To the extent that * **Kanu yistakhdimooh** (چانوا يستخدموه) - They used to use it * **Sometimes** (sometimes - often borrowed directly) * **Yizakhrufoon** (يزخرفون) - They decorate * **Al-Suwar** (الصور) - The pictures * **Al-Marsouma** (المرسومة) - Painted/Drawn * **Bil-eed** (بالإيد) - By hand * **Bil-kutub** (بالكتب) - In the books * **Al-Musamma** (المسمّاة) - Called/Named * **Al-Manshoorat** (المنشورات) - The manuscripts/illuminations * **Al-Mudhiya'a** (المضيئة) - The illuminated/bright. **Important Notes:** * **Regional Variation:** Mesopotamian Arabic isn't a single, uniform language. It encompasses many dialects. This translation leans towards a common, central Iraqi (Baghdadi) influence, attempting to be relatively understandable across the region. * **Loanwords:** The inclusion of "sometimes" is common. Mesopotamian Arabic frequently borrows words when a direct equivalent isn't readily available or feels clunky. * **'Illuminated Manuscripts'**: Translating concepts like "illuminated manuscripts" can be challenging. I've broken it down to "manuscripts that are bright/illuminated". The nuance of artistic technique may be lost in a direct translation. * **Grammatical Structure:** The sentence structure is adjusted to sound natural in Mesopotamian Arabic. Word order differs from English.

خلّط البودرة الناشفة الاثنين مع بعضها بشكل دوّار، وبعدين بأيديك المبلّلة والنظيفة، اعجنها/ضمّها لكرّة. (Khallaṭ al-būdra an-nāshfa al-itnayn maʿa baʿḍiha bi-shakl duwwār, wa baʿdayn bi-īdīk al-muballala wan-naẓīfa, aʿjin-ha/ḍumm-ha li-kurra.) **Notes on choices and nuance:** * **“Swirl”** is best captured by "بشكل دوّار" (bi-shakl duwwār) - “in a swirling manner.” * **“Dry powders”** is “البودرة الناشفة” (al-būdra an-nāshfa) - "the dry powder." Using the definite article is common in instructions. * **"squeeze into a ball"** has two options: “اعجنها” (aʿjin-ha) meaning "knead it" - more appropriate for something pliable - *or* “ضمّها” (ḍumm-ha) meaning "compress/gather it" - better if the powders don't easily mold. I've given both, separated by a slash, as the best choice depends on the material being described. * **"Clean wet hands"** is "أيديك المبلّلة والنظيفة" (īdīk al-muballala wan-naẓīfa) - “your wet and clean hands." The order is more natural this way in Mesopotamian Arabic.

باخير، اكو هواي قطط صغار (بيهم القطط الضالة اللي متربّية) ياكلون فريسة صغيرة بكثرة، مثل الحشرات، الجرذان، السحالي، والطيور. (Bakhir, اكو hwayy qṭṭaṣ ṣġār (bihum al-qiṭṭaṣ al-ḍālla illi mitrabbāyah) yakloon frīsah ṣġīrah bikathrah, mithl al-ḥasharāt, al-jirdān, al-suḥālī, wa al-ṭuyūr.)
